< Text>
Hummus and schnitzel have rarely been so delicious as at Village Hummus. What a random but great find thanks to Yelp.

You'll see Village Hummus tucked into a mall/apartment complex with some limited street parking. Come in and the store looks fairly inconspicuous - a few tables (it's fairly small). Order at the counter with a few different variations on the dishes like pita variations to plate variations - it's a super straightforward menu. I went with the schnitzel and hummus for about $9ish.

When the plate came out, you get a good amount of food. Along with the hummus/schnitzel you'll get a couple big pita breads, chopped salad, pickles, tahini and lemon relish. You can also get the optional hot sauce dip (forgot the exact name here) which is actually pretty spicy but deliciously so. The hummus is plentiful and is made just right. The schnitzel is also fairly large and delicious.

Staff was super kind with some limited drink options. Definitely seems like a neighborhood kind of vibe. Really enjoyed it and hope to come back again soon when I'm in the area.</Text>

<time>1584661977253<//time><rating>5<//rating><Review>Great historical building with interesting architectural details. Fun place to walk around or sit and watch the bay. Not too big for the less mobile people, but contains a decent variety of food stalls and shops in addition to the actual ferry ports. The farmers markets are a fun place to meet and have coffee as the morning weather on the Embarcadero is generally exquisite most of the year. Besides the fresh produce there are multiple vendors offering prepared foods. One of the unique experiences to see in San Francisco on Saturday mornings 8a-2p (also Tu/Th 10-2) and relatively easy by public transit. One of those places where locals and tourists mix.</Review>< Pics>

< Rate>
5<//Rate>
<text>Attention all foodies: this delectable attraction needs to be at the top of your San Francisco to-do list. The Ferry Building Marketplace is a public food market that features a variety of food stalls that act as small restaurants, snack stops and grocery stores. Here you can find everything from staples, such as seafood, burgers, Mexican food and plenty of coffee, to a Japanese delicatessen, empanada stand, nut shop and a cheese and dairy bar.

Many travelers who stopped by the Ferry Building Marketplace visited multiple times during their San Francisco trip. Visitors were impressed with the amount, variety and overall quality of eats available on-site. Though there are formal restaurants available, some visitors say the best strategy is to pick up a to-go meal and enjoy it along the scenic waterfront. And if you're not one for lines, don't come on the weekends.

You can reach the marketplace via the Embarcadero BART/Muni Station and several public buses lines. Parking is also available near the marketplace. The marketplace is open daily from 10 a.m. to 7 p.m with slightly different hours on the weekends. Restaurants and stores, however, maintain varied hours. The farmers market welcomes shoppers from 10 a.m. to 2 p.m. Tuesdays and Thursdays and from 8 a.m. to 2 p.m. on Saturdays.</text><pictures>None< /pictures><response>None</response>< Gmap_id>

<rating>5<//rating><Review>My husband and I are parents of 4 children who are students attending this school. One of which is on the spectrum and special needs. Though we (our son, his teachers, school staff, my husband and I) have had a lot of difficult days and many I.E.P./school meetings...overall, I think this school deserves the highest rating possible (which on here would be a 5). The teachers we have had so far are amazing (for all 4 of our kids) and you can tell they want the best for their students and genuinely care about each child's progress.

R.A.G. (Rocklin Academy Gateway) has received a lot of negative publicity in the last couple years over following the law by keeping the identity and privacy of a transgender Kindergarten student protected. When we saw the news about a transgender ceremony and book reading, we too were initially concerned, especially since we had a Kindergartner attending there. We were able to sort out, to the best of our knowledge, what actually transpired without specific details on whom or when that the ceremony was the normal Kindergarten graduation ceremony, not a transgender reveal. The book, albeit perhaps not advisable to read to 5 and 6 year olds who may or may not understand what gender is yet...was on the approved reading list and brought by the student; not specifically selected by the teacher. However, personal opinions on what 'could' have been done differently aside...even in the midst of heightened media attention, threats, controversy and adverse student body responses...the school maintained their stance and followed state law. Even if you disagree with the political or social controversy you can be certain of this fact...they will protect your child, your family's identity and provide a safe environment for the student NO MATTER WHAT. I respect that and applaud them for their composure through the entire ordeal. We NEED MORE SCHOOLS LIKE THIS ONE!</Review>< pictures>

<userid>103283854179864298843<//userid>< username>
Krysta Dancy< /username>
<Time>1507772328599< /Time>< rate>
5< /rate>
< review>
Our child has been attending since this campus opened. While the school has had a normal amount of growing pains (like traffic issues) overall we are so pleased with the school. The school is quick to accommodate special needs. The administration is very responsive and takes safety and bullying issues seriously.
I volunteer in class and see first hand how well they tailor the instruction to each child's individual skill level. They arrange the grade levels around "hubs" or flexible use areas. This allows them to shift students for every lesson (math, spelling etc) and each teacher takes a class-sized group of similar skill level. Within the groups they break into three smaller skill-level groups. Each child's skill level is adjusted throughout the year as needed. I am so impressed with how well the kids learn this way!
Additionally, their curriculum is impressive. They use a curriculum that "wraps around" each year. So kids will see the same subject matter to greater depths each year (like the human body, or immigration). We feel so lucky we made it in the lottery.

Recent press attention, much of it inaccurate,  and the opening of a middle school seems to have drawn some commentary here. Ha! But in terms of 1. Rigorous Academics 2. Safe school 3. Responsive Administration... I'm incredibly pleased.<//review>

<UserId.>103036444109630190274<//UserId.>< review>
Love this authentic Sri Lankan cuisine!!< /review>
<Time>1479672982641</Time></record></dataset><record>
< user_id>
105752952950814313225<//user_id>
<Name>Raz & Imbri P<//Name><Time>1579943003162</Time><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Neither of us had tried Sri Lankan food before, so when we crossed the strip-mall parking lot to the unassuming little restaurant almost tucked away in the corner, we had no idea at all what to expect. The simple, no-frills dining room and long warming tray display of unfamiliar dishes along the front next to the register told us that any longevity for this business would rely entirely on the food. The aromas were incredible, though, so we had instantly high hopes.

Our hopes were slightly dashed when we heard that none of the mutton dishes were still on the menu, but Raz ordered one beef and one veg dish from those on display with some rice, and I put in an order for Godamba Roti, and asked for suggestions on which meat and veg curry to pair it with. Godamba Roti appears to be a crepe-like flatbread that has an indescribably complex flavor. Alas, I did not write down any of the names of the sides and curries, and I couldn't even remember what I'd actually ordered when it came to the table. All I did know was that I'd never had anything else quite like it. Every single dish we had defied explanation, being simply too rich with complex and complementary flavors. One thing was certain, though, when the staff promised a dish was spicy, it pleasantly packed on the scovilles. Rice N' Spice was definitely one of those places we would come back halfway across the country to try again.</review>

5) Washing machines usually have human and pet hair in them from the previous person who used the machine.

<Review>I moved I in September last year. I got very discouraged after reading the reviews but not having any credit to go for a different option I decided to go for it and I'm really surprised! Im about to relocate and I don't have anything bad to say for what I chose!

I got one of the renovated one bedrooms apartments. They have been upgrading the building here and there making it better to live in (they changed all the toilets and all the windows since I moved in) and whenever I had a problem maintenance was ready to help !

It is pricy but so are most of the places around LA and considering they don't ask for an arm and a leg as deposit and that all utilities are included, the deal is not that bad. Of course.. Coming from a smaller city like I did the rent still feels overpriced, but so does every single one bedroom apartment in and around LA.

Management has been great. I also think it has a lot to do with the attitude you go about any issue.
